# Bugs Remaining — Signacare EMR

_Updated 2026-05-28. Source-of-truth for open work before Azure staging cutover._

**Authority:** [`governance-control-plane.md`](governance-control-plane.md) §2. This document supersedes `docs/archive/audit-2026-04-19/bug-catalogue-v2.yaml` for triage decisions. The catalogue yaml is retained as the structured machine-readable history and MUST be kept in sync when a bug transitions state. If the two disagree, THIS file wins until the yaml is updated in the same PR.

**CSV mirror:** [`bugs-remaining-2026-05-24.csv`](bugs-remaining-2026-05-24.csv) — full programmatic mirror of Sections 2 + 3 + 4 below. The older `bugs-remaining-2026-05-23.csv` is preserved in place as a dated snapshot.

## Section 1 — Legend + Schema

### Legend

- **Severity** — S0 (patient-safety or compliance-blocker) / S1 (deploy-blocker) / S2 (should-ship-before-GA) / S3 (tech-debt, can land after staging).
- **State** — `open`, `in_progress`, `blocked_external` (gated on non-engineering event), `deferred` (explicit decision to postpone with a stated re-visit trigger), `paused` (engineering in-flight, awaiting a prerequisite), `fixed` (closed with evidence).
- **Pre/Post deployment** — `pre` (must close before Azure/canary deployment) or `post` (deferred to post-deployment hardening). Per-row label; not section-implicit anymore.
- **Owner** — accountable individual / team. Empty (`—`) = unassigned (operator/leads to fill).
- **Evidence link** — path to `docs/quality/remediation/evidence/<file>.md` if closure evidence exists; empty for open/in-progress rows (the evidence will be added at closure time). See unresolved-gap list in d14 §6.
- **Next action** — the concrete remaining step to move the row toward closure (or, for `deferred` rows, the defer trigger + the eventual action).

### Schema (canonical 8 columns for Sections 2 / 3 / 4)

```
| Bug ID | Area/Workflow | Severity | State | Pre/Post deployment | Owner | Evidence link | Next action |
```

### Pre-Deployment Closure Lock (As Of 2026-05-28)

1. Azure/canary deployment has **not started**.
2. Code-completion bugs are closed in this ledger when deterministic local L1-L5 evidence is green.
3. External canary/burn-in checks are tracked as rollout operations and must remain explicit in deployment runbooks.

### Restructure note (2026-05-24)

This file was restructured on 2026-05-24 per the operator's S0-first directive. The active ledger now lives in Sections 2 (S0-pre), 3 (S1-pre), 4 (post-deployment), and 5 (superseded). The pre-2026-05-24 legacy by-severity and audit-wave content is preserved in **Section 6 — Reference Archive (NON-AUTHORITATIVE)** below, with a top-of-section disclaimer. Rows from the legacy sections that were CURRENTLY OPEN and not already represented in Sections 2/3 were promoted to the new active sections (e.g., legacy BUG-344 and BUG-P1 moved from legacy "S0 — Must fix before staging" into Section 2). Strikethrough/closed rows in the legacy sections remain in Section 6 for audit-trail continuity. See [`d14-doc-cleanup-backlog-reorg-s0-2026-05-24.md`](remediation/evidence/d14-doc-cleanup-backlog-reorg-s0-2026-05-24.md) for the full evidence packet.

| BUG-377-FOLLOWUP-NIL-PLACEHOLDER-AMBIGUITY | S2 | (BUG-377 L4 cycle-2 advisory; surfaced 2026-05-03) The MSE completeness gate treats `nil` as a not-assessed placeholder. Australian psychiatrists commonly write `nil suicidal ideation` or `nil perceptual abnormality` as a POSITIVE clinical finding meaning "I asked, nothing found" — which should count as ASSESSED. A bare `nil` in `thoughtContent` will currently be treated as not-assessed even when the clinician used it as a documented finding. Fix shape: post-merge sample audit on 50-100 historical signed consultations to verify the `nil`/`none` treatment matches clinical intent; if false-positives occur, either (a) remove `nil`/`none` from `NOT_ASSESSED_PLACEHOLDERS` and require `not assessed` / `n/a` etc. as the explicit unassessed marker, OR (b) add UX hint in the form ("Use 'No abnormality detected' instead of 'nil' to indicate a positive negative finding"). Monitoring lever: track 422 `MSE_INCOMPLETE_FOR_SIGN` errors per clinician — outliers indicate either training gap or false-positive. Filed atomically per `feedback_no_silent_out_of_scope.md`. |
| ~~BUG-377~~ | **fixed** | ~~MSE completeness check — block sign with ≥ 8/10 `not_assessed` domains~~ — Closed 2026-05-03 (Bucket A Tier-C drain). NEW `apps/api/src/features/clinical-review/mseCompletenessGate.ts` — boundary gate `assertMseCompletenessOnSign(mse, status)` that fires ONLY on status='signed' transitions. Threshold: ≥ 8 of 11 MSE domains not_assessed → throw `AppError(422, 'MSE_INCOMPLETE_FOR_SIGN', { assessed, notAssessed, totalDomains, skippedDomains })`. "Not assessed" = null / empty / whitespace-only / canonical placeholders ("not assessed", "n/a", "nil", "—", "?", etc., case-insensitive). Drafts may be arbitrarily sparse during composition; signing locks the record per AHPRA Standard 1 forensic posture. Wired at the repository boundary (`clinicalReviewRepository.createConsultation` + `updateConsultation`); the updateConsultation path reads existing row's mse to determine the FINAL state when caller doesn't pass mse (e.g. transition to 'signed' without re-supplying mse). 20 unit tests at `apps/api/tests/unit/mseCompletenessGate.test.ts` covering: domain-assessed predicate (4 placeholder classes), domain-count helper (full/null/partial), gate happy-path (full + 4-assessed boundary), gate reject-path (0/1/2 assessed + error details + skipped-domain list), draft/in_progress/cancelled status passthrough, placeholder substitution (all 11 fields placeholder → 0 assessed → reject), threshold constants pinned. **Scope note**: catalogue text said "8/10" but the actual schema has 11 domains; we apply the same absolute count (8) yielding ~73% threshold which honors catalogue intent (most-domains-skipped = not-real-MSE). | BUG-394 | **fixed** | ~~AI scribe draft does NOT cross-check prescribed drug against patient_allergies.~~ — Closed atomically: NEW `apps/api/src/features/medications/allergyMatching.ts` SSoT for CLASS_MATRIX (β-lactam / sulfa / NSAID per Australian Medicines Handbook) + `normaliseAllergen` + `allergensCrossReactingWith` matcher. `checkContraindications.ts` refactored to import the canonical matcher (102 LOC removed, no behaviour change). NEW `apps/api/src/mcp/scribeAllergyAssessor.ts` — pure-function `assessAllergies(verifiedMedications, allergyRows)` returning `SafetyAlert[]` + load-and-assess wrapper `assessAllergiesForAmbientPipeline(clinicId, patientId, verifiedMedications)` for the ambient pipeline. Pass-2 in `ambientProcessor.ts` wires the wrapper after `verifyMedications`; allergy alerts merge into the existing safetyAlerts array (same UI surface as dose-range / monitoring / risk alerts). `medicalScribe.ts` re-exports `assessAllergies` + `AllergyContextRow` for backwards compatibility. **Locked design decisions**: cross-check fires ONLY for prescribing-intent (`change` ∈ {started, increased, continued, decreased, ceased}; 'mentioned' excluded to avoid false-positives from "we discussed her penicillin allergy"); severe \| anaphylaxis → critical, all else → warning (conservative); reaction text included in alert message; allergen_type='drug' + status='active' + deleted_at IS NULL filtered upstream by repository. **Tests**: 12 unit tests TP-AAC-1..12 — 3× flake GREEN. **L1**: tsc × 3 workspaces clean; 27 guards GREEN; 1209 fix-registry anchors verified (1201 + 8 BUG-394). **L2**: 12/12 unit tests 3× flake; 0 regressions vs baseline (7 pre-existing baseline failures unchanged). **L3 cycle 1 PASS**, **L4 cycle 1 PASS** (2 medium-residual follow-ups filed as 394-FOLLOWUP-3/4), **L5 cycle 1 PASS** all 5 standards. 4 cascade BUGs filed atomically (394b/c/d/e — see below). SHA pending. |
| BUG-394b | S2 | (BUG-394 plan + L4 cycle-1 follow-up) Cephalosporin↔penicillin cross-reactivity in `CLASS_MATRIX`. 2026 literature mixed — historical estimate 5-10% cross-reactivity is contested by recent meta-analyses showing <2% for current-generation cephalosporins (modified side chain). Decision: extend matrix or document explicit non-coverage in clinical-safety review. Pre-fix coverage gap is patient_allergies.allergen='penicillin' + prescribed='cefalexin' produces NO alert (false-negative). Filed atomically with BUG-394 close. |
| BUG-394c | S2 | (BUG-394 plan + L5 cycle-1 follow-up) Hard sign-off block on critical allergy alerts. v1 surfaces the alert but does NOT block sign-off (consistent with how dose-range critical alerts behave today). A clinician CAN sign through a critical alert. Decision needed: introduce a hard UI gate that requires explicit override + audit_log entry before sign-off proceeds. Mirrors the prescribing-path's existing CONTRAINDICATION_OVERRIDE_REQUIRED audit-log convention but at the scribe-draft surface. Filed atomically with BUG-394 close. |
| BUG-394d | S2 | (BUG-394 L4 cycle-1 medium-residual) Pass-1 `change='mentioned'` false-negative class. `verifyMedications` defaults `change` to 'mentioned' when the change-verb regex doesn't match. A clinician dictating *"amoxicillin 500mg BD"* without an explicit verb (started/commenced/etc.) → Pass-1 emits `[M] amoxicillin 500mg BD` → Pass-2 marks `change='mentioned'` → cross-check is silently skipped (TP-AAC-4 design — exclude 'mentioned'). Coronial review of "wrong drug despite recorded allergy" would find the cross-check ran but emitted no alert. Mitigation: treat unmarked medication mentions as `'started'` for cross-check purposes only (NOT for note formatting), OR widen the change regex, OR mandate Pass-1 system prompt enforcement. Filed atomically with BUG-394 close. |
| BUG-394e | S2 | (BUG-394 L4 cycle-1 medium-residual) Persist `safetyAlerts` array to a structured column on `clinical_notes` (e.g. `clinical_notes.safety_alerts JSONB`). Currently the alerts are returned in the API response and threaded into Pass-3 prompt but NOT persisted as a structured column — coronial reviewer reconstructing "did the system warn the clinician about this allergy?" must rely on the ephemeral response payload OR the LLM-mediated Pass-3 note text. The dose_range / monitoring / risk alerts share this gap; this is a system-wide forensic concern, not BUG-394-specific. Filed atomically with BUG-394 close. |

| BUG-400e | S2 | (BUG-400 L4 cycle-1 residual) Auto-expire of legal_orders happens INSIDE a GET handler at `apps/api/src/features/patients/patientRoutes.ts:822-830` (every list-orders read flips past-end-date orders to `status='expired'`). This conflates a side-effect with a read endpoint; the actor on the audit trail (if BUG-400d lands) becomes the GET caller, not "system" — and a clinician opening a patient mid-renewal can silently expire an in-force order before the new one is filed. Fix: move auto-expire to the existing `mhaReviewScheduler` (or a sibling daily cron) using `dbAdmin`, emit `audit_log` with `actor_staff_id: 'system'` sentinel + `auto_expired_by: 'cron'` metadata. | BUG-401 | S2 | Per-clinic configurable MHA review-window (pair with BUG-372) |
| BUG-402 | **fixed** | ~~No optimistic locking on ECT/TMS `treatment_pathways.milestones` JSONB~~ — Closed atomically: migration `20260701000038_bug_402_treatment_pathways_lock_version.ts` adds `lock_version int NOT NULL DEFAULT 1` (builder-first, idempotent, no-op down per BUG-371 / clinical_notes precedent); NEW `apps/api/src/features/treatment-pathways/pathwayRepository.ts` extracted from inline routes encapsulates JSONB shallow-merge then routes through the BUG-371a `updateWithOptimisticLock` helper; `pathwayRoutes.ts` PATCH `/:id` and POST `/:id/session` consume the repository so concurrent +1 session calls cannot silently overwrite (first wins, second 409 OPTIMISTIC_LOCK_CONFLICT). **Asymmetric Zod posture: REQUIRED `expectedLockVersion`** at the boundary on `UpdateTreatmentPathwaySchema` and `RecordSessionSchema` — only 2 web mutators (PathwaysTab, PathwaysPage), zero mobile/external clients, atomic flip safe (no transition shim needed unlike episodes). `TreatmentPathwayResponseSchema` includes REQUIRED `lockVersion` so clients echo it. | BUG-AZURE-WINDOWS-VM-FOLLOWUP-BICEP-SENTINEL-VALIDATION | S3 | (BUG-AZURE-WINDOWS-VM L5 advisory #4; surfaced 2026-05-03) `rdpAllowedSource` defaults to sentinel `'REPLACE_ME_WITH_CORPORATE_IP_CIDR'` which Azure NSG CIDR validation rejects at deploy time — fail-fast behaviour relies on Azure-layer validation. **2026-05-03 investigation**: Bicep stable does NOT have a clean parameter-rejection mechanism. The `assert` keyword (Bicep 0.27.1+) requires the experimental `assertions` feature to be enabled via `bicepconfig.json`, which forces operators onto recent Bicep CLI versions AND complicates the deploy posture for orgs with default tooling. Other approaches considered + rejected: (a) `@allowed([...])` — sentinel must be one of the values to default to it, can't enumerate all valid CIDRs; (b) `parseCidr()` builtin to force parse failure — not stable across all Bicep versions; (c) nested deployment with `if`-condition — overengineered for a fail-fast belt. Conclusion: Azure NSG CIDR validation remains load-bearing; Bicep-level belt deferred until Bicep stabilises a non-experimental assert primitive. Non-blocking because Azure-layer rejection IS load-bearing today. |

Group 1 has RLS mitigation; Group 2 has NO mitigation (real cross-tenant write authorization gap with no current defense). The 6 INSERT call sites already write `clinic_id` for Group 1; for Group 2 they write `staff_id` only (no `clinic_id` to write — schema doesn't have it). **Filed atomically with batch-6a commit per operator authorization 2026-05-06**: discovery + catalogue update landed together (commit a9b295f); BUG row updated 2026-05-06 to reflect Group 1 / Group 2 split per operator-authorized fix scope (c). |
| ~~BUG-EPISODE-MDT-SAVE-RACE~~ | **fixed** | (Discovered 2026-05-06 by L4 clinical-safety-reviewer cycle-2 audit during BUG-STAFF-SETTINGS-CLINIC-ID-FILTER closure; **pre-existing concurrency defect, NOT introduced by the closure fix**); **CLOSED 2026-05-06** via operator-authorized scope (B) + L4 cycle-1 absorb option (a) + L5 cycle-1 absorb option (A). **Defect class (refined post-L5 cycle-1, 2026-05-06): cross-handler concurrency closure on the (clinic_id, org_unit_id) lock domain + restoration of effective-dating semantics on the deactivate transition.** Two writer surfaces participate in the lock domain: (1) `episodeRoutes.ts POST /:id/allocate` critical section (lines 152-280 pre-fix) now wrapped in `db.transaction(async (trx) => { ... })` with `pg_advisory_xact_lock(hashtext(clinicId || ':' || orgUnitId))` acquired at the start; all queries inside use `trx` per CLAUDE.md §2.1. Workflow event emission moved post-commit (outside the transaction; failure should not roll back MDT save). (2) **L5 cycle-1 absorb (option A)**: `referralRoutes.ts POST /:id/allocate` (lines 255-339 pre-fix) now wraps the same critical-section shape in `db.transaction` + `pg_advisory_xact_lock(hashtext(clinicId || ':' || orgUnitId))` with **identical lock-key shape and parameters** as episodeRoutes — so the two handlers serialize against each other on shared (clinic_id, org_unit_id) writes. Intake-episode close stays POST-commit (outside the transaction). Without this absorb, a referral-allocate concurrent with an episode-allocate could interleave with the episode's deactivate-then-insert sequence, producing chaotic mid-race states (size-3 active row outcomes when 2 distinct 2-row compositions interleave); with both handlers in the same lock domain, post-fix outcomes are deterministic E-then-R (size 4) or R-then-E (size 2), never mid-race. **L4 cycle-1 absorb (option a)**: the deactivate UPDATE on `staff_role_assignments` (episodeRoutes.ts line 222-224) now also sets `end_date = today` alongside `is_active = false`, restoring effective-dating semantics for AHPRA Standard 8 record-keeping + coronial review point-in-time queries. Pre-fix posture deactivated rows were left with `end_date IS NULL` despite logical termination — silent corruption of the temporal audit trail; addressed inline (not via separate BUG) because it lives on the exact deactivate state-transition line being modified. NEW integration test `bugEpisodeMdtSaveRace.int.test.ts` carries 3/3 PASS: (1) concurrent `Promise.all([req1(compositionA), req2(compositionB)])` for same episode + org_unit returns 200 on both; final active set is EXACTLY one composition (last-writer-wins) with NO duplicate (staff_id, clinical_role_id) active rows; (2) sequential A→B saves leave deactivated A-staff rows with `is_active=false` AND `end_date IS NOT NULL`; (3) **cross-handler race**: concurrent `Promise.all([episode-allocate(E), referral-allocate(R)])` for same (clinic_id, org_unit_id) returns 200 on both; final active staff_id set is EXACTLY one of the two valid serialized outcomes (E-then-R: size 4 = E∪R; R-then-E: size 2 = E only); explicitly NOT size 3 (chaotic mid-race state pre-fix could have observed). SHA pending. Pre-fix history below for record: `apps/api/src/features/episode/episodeRoutes.ts:194-276` performs `POST /episodes/:id/allocate` MDT save as a deactivate-then-insert loop OUTSIDE a transaction. Sequence: (1) UPDATE all role_type='additional' assignments for the org_unit to is_active=false (line 194-196); (2) iterate the DTO's MDT roles and either reactivate-existing or insert-new assignments. **Race window**: two simultaneous `POST /episodes/:id/allocate` calls for the same `(clinic_id, org_unit_id)` can interleave — T1 deactivation → T2 deactivation → T1 INSERTs → T2 INSERTs — producing the union of both clinicians' MDT rows (possible duplicates) or stale role attribution between deactivation and insertion. **Clinical consequence**: brief stale clinician on the MDT roster during the race window; potential duplicate role attribution rows post-race; observable as inconsistent MDT display in the UI immediately after concurrent saves. **Fix shape**: wrap lines 194-276 in `db.transaction(async (trx) => { ... })` per CLAUDE.md §2.1, OR add an advisory lock on `(clinic_id, org_unit_id)` via `pg_advisory_xact_lock(hashtext(clinic_id || org_unit_id))`, OR add an idempotency key on the request (request-side dedup). The transaction approach is the canonical fix; CLAUDE.md §2.1 explicitly mandates "Every query inside a transaction MUST use the transaction object" and the deactivate-then-insert sequence is the textbook case. **Severity S2**: clinical workflow integrity (MDT attribution); concurrency-only — no patient-harm class without the race actually triggering. RLS belt + clinic_id filter (now in place per BUG-STAFF-SETTINGS-CLINIC-ID-FILTER closure) prevent cross-tenant interleaving; the S2 race is intra-clinic concurrent MDT saves. **Filed atomically with BUG-STAFF-SETTINGS-CLINIC-ID-FILTER closure** per operator authorization 2026-05-06 + `feedback_no_silent_out_of_scope.md` (concrete file:line = concrete enough to file; silent parking is the anti-pattern this rule prevents). |

| BUG-403-FOLLOWUP-OPTIONS-OBJECT-REFACTOR | S2 | (BUG-403-FOLLOWUP-CONFIG-WRITE-AUDIT L5 advisory; surfaced 2026-05-03) `settingsService.setThreshold` now has 6 positional parameters: `(clinicId, key, value, conn?, skipRelationalCheck?, actorStaffId?)`. | BUG-403-FOLLOWUP-AUDIT-TRANSACTION | S2 | (BUG-403-FOLLOWUP-CONFIG-WRITE-AUDIT L5 advisory; surfaced 2026-05-03) `setThreshold` audit path is a 3-step SELECT/upsert/SELECT/audit sequence not wrapped in a transaction. A concurrent writer between the upsert and the post-image re-read could cause the audit row's `newData.threshold_value` to disagree with the row's actual current state (the post-image SELECT sees the OTHER writer's value, not the one this caller just wrote). Concrete impact small — paired keys are protected by `bulkSetThresholds` controller pre-validation; the actorStaffId-supplied path is realistic-serial-by-actor — but for correctness invariant the whole 4-step block (capture pre, upsert, capture post, emit audit) should be wrapped in `conn.transaction(async (trx) => { ... })`. Sibling pattern of CLAUDE.md §2.1 transaction discipline. Filed atomically per `feedback_no_silent_out_of_scope.md`. |
| BUG-403-FOLLOWUP-DB-CHECK-CONSTRAINT | S2 | (BUG-403 cycle-2 L4 BLOCK absorb residual; surfaced 2026-05-03) Layer A (service-level guards) is in place; Layer B (DB CHECK constraint) is missing. The `clinic_thresholds.threshold_value` column accepts any numeric value at the DB level — defence-in-depth posture per CLAUDE.md §17.4 (Zod L1 + service L2 + DB CHECK L3) requires a constraint that DB-side rejects out-of-bounds writes for clinical-safety-load-bearing keys. Fix shape: NEW migration adding partial CHECK constraint shape `CHECK (threshold_key NOT IN ('clozapine_anc_red_threshold','clozapine_anc_amber_threshold') OR (threshold_key = 'clozapine_anc_red_threshold' AND threshold_value BETWEEN 1.5 AND 5.0) OR (threshold_key = 'clozapine_anc_amber_threshold' AND threshold_value BETWEEN 2.0 AND 5.0))`. NOT urgent because Layer A blocks all known write paths (only `setThreshold` writes; service is a small surface); Layer B is belt-below-suspenders for direct SQL bypass / future writer authors who don't go through the service. Filed atomically per `feedback_no_silent_out_of_scope.md`. |

| BUG-552 | S2 | NPDS callback orphan-eRx-token risk (BUG-371b absorb-1 L4 finding). `prescriptionService.submitErx` reads `row.lock_version` BEFORE the NPDS round-trip; on opt-lock conflict during the round-trip, the helper throws AppError(409) and `prescriptions.erx_token` is NOT persisted — but `erx_tokens` row IS still INSERTed at line 241-249 (separate INSERT, not opt-locked). Result: an issued eScript with a real NPDS token can land in `erx_tokens` while `prescriptions.erx_token` stays NULL — orphan eScript visible only via JOIN + audit. Fix shape per plan §2.5.5: wrap the read+update in `db.transaction(async (trx) => { const row = await trx('prescriptions').forUpdate().first(); ... await updateWithOptimisticLock({..., trx}); })`. The `FOR UPDATE` makes the read+update atomic; the helper's predicate then degenerates to a tautology but keeps the version increment consistent. Surfaced by BUG-371b absorb-1 L4 review. |

| BUG-424d | S3 | (BUG-424 L5 cycle-1 Standard 3 advisory) `WHISPER_API_URL` is duplicated 6 times across `llmRoutes.ts:1002,1021`, `streamingTranscribeRoutes.ts:34`, `psychiatristFeatureRoutes.ts:504`, `scribeStreaming.ts:62`, `ambientProcessor.ts:62`, `whisperClient.ts:47`. | BUG-424e | S2 | (BUG-424 L5 cycle-1 architectural advisory) `apps/api/src/mcp/ambientProcessor.ts` is 1290 LOC and concentrates Whisper inference, diarization, Pass-1/Pass-2 LLM, MSE extraction, risk flagging, formatting, and now Whisper audit-row writing. Test fixtures (1 patient + 1 episode + N clinical_notes per run) accumulate harmlessly with fresh per-run UUIDs. **Live-DB demonstrate-pass: 6/6 tests PASS in <1s on port 5433. BUG-451 batch 7 of 7+ completed 2026-05-02 — ALL 7 PLANNED BATCHES NOW CLOSED**. |
| BUG-424b-FOLLOWUP-METADATA-PHI-RATIONALE | S3 | (BUG-424b L4 advisory cycle-1 retroactive review 2026-05-01) Document in CLAUDE.md or `docs/quality/audit-row-phi-policy.md` that `transcriptLength` integer in `llm_interactions.metadata` is forensic signal, NOT PHI per HPP/AHPRA definitions. Pre-empts future challenge that "a length value plus a known patient_id could narrow inference for short transcripts (e.g. 4-character 'yes'/'no')". Rationale: (a) length is not "personal information" under Privacy Act 1988 sec 6, (b) `metadata.transcriptLength` is sufficient signal for forensic dashboards (e.g. detecting truncated-transcription failure modes) without crossing into PHI, (c) the actual transcript content lives in `clinical_notes.content` under separate AHPRA Standard 6 record-keeping discipline. Filed atomically with BUG-424b close. |

| BUG-491 | STRUCTURAL | `apps/api/src/features/patient-app/patientAppRoutes.ts` is dual-purpose — same file houses patient-app self-service handlers AND clinician-facing handlers (clinician POSTs invites, sets med-reminders/thresholds for patients on `VivaTab.tsx`). The file path `features/patient-app/` reads as patient-app-only. The dual-use was the root cause of BUG-430-PATIENT-APP's REJECT-1: a developer assumed all handlers in this file received only patient-app JWTs, broke 30 clinician call sites. Fix shape: split into (a) `patientAppRoutes.ts` for true patient-app self-service routes, (b) `vivaPlatformRoutes.ts` for clinician-facing Viva CRUD. Mounted at separate URL prefixes (`/patient-app/*` and `/patients/:patientId/viva/*`). Filed during BUG-430-PATIENT-APP REJECT-1 absorb. |
| BUG-492 | S2 | Invariant test for `req.user.clinicId === req.clinicId` post-authMiddleware. Two sources of clinic context exist in every authed request: the JWT claim (`req.user.clinicId`) and the tenantMiddleware-set `req.clinicId`. They SHOULD always agree but no automated test asserts it. The `requirePatientOwnership` helper at L470 had a `tokenClinicId = user?.clinicId ?? req.clinicId` fallback that masked the disagreement axis (now corrected in absorb to `||` strict-equal). File a unit/integration test that walks every authed handler and asserts `req.user.clinicId === req.clinicId`. Closes a class of cross-tenant subtleties. Filed during BUG-430-PATIENT-APP REJECT-1 absorb. |
| BUG-493 | S2 | `PATCH /api/v1/patient-app/assessments/:patientId/:assessmentId/complete` does not assert `WHERE status = 'pending'`. A patient could re-PATCH a `completed` assessment, overwriting their original PHQ-9/GAD-7 responses and total_score. Append-only invariant violation per CLAUDE.md §1 (clinical data is append-only). Pre-existing (not introduced by BUG-430-PATIENT-APP). Fix shape: add `.where({ status: 'pending' })` to the UPDATE; on no-row return 409 ASSESSMENT_ALREADY_COMPLETE. Filed during BUG-430-PATIENT-APP REJECT-1 absorb (L4 surface). |
| BUG-494 | S3 | `apps/api/src/shared/authGuards.ts:572` uses `await import('./buildAuthContext')` with rationale "circular-import-avoidance" — but `buildAuthContext.ts` does NOT import `authGuards.ts`, so a static import would work. The dynamic import (a) hides the dependency from `dependency-cruiser`, (b) defers any import-time error to first request, (c) adds tiny per-call overhead. Fix shape: replace with top-of-file `import { buildAuthContext } from './buildAuthContext';` after `npx depcruise --validate` confirms no cycle. Filed during BUG-430-PATIENT-APP REJECT-1 absorb (L5 surface). |
| BUG-496 | S3 | `apps/api/src/shared/authGuards.ts` LOC trend approaching the 600-LOC warn threshold (now 575 after BUG-430-PATIENT-APP). The file is a god-collection of all service-layer auth guards (`requirePermission`, `requireClinicMatch`, `requireSpecialty`, `requirePrescribingDiscipline`, `requireValidHpii`, `requirePatientRelationship`, `requireClinicalAccessRole`, `requireAccessSettingsAuthority`, `requirePatientOwnership`). | BUG-497 | S2 | Extend `scripts/guards/check-patient-app-ownership.ts` to scan ALL mutating routes (POST/PUT/PATCH/DELETE) in patientAppRoutes.ts, not just `:patientId`-keyed paths. Currently the guard only fires on routes whose path contains `:patientId`; entry-id-keyed routes (`:entryId`, `:appointmentId`, `:reminderId`, `:thresholdId`, `:checklistId`, `:assessmentId`) are uncovered. BUG-490 closed 3 such sites manually; a future engineer adding a 4th would not be CI-blocked. Fix shape: per-route-param column-binding table mapping `:entryId` → `patient_tracking`, `:appointmentId` → `appointments`, etc.; require either (a) WHERE clause keyed by `req.params.patientId` with the helper, OR (b) explicit SELECT-then-helper pattern, OR (c) `@patient-app-ownership-exempt` annotation. Filed during BUG-490 §I L5 review. |
| BUG-498 | S2 | Surface a `truncated: true` flag on every list endpoint where BUG-437 ceilings can fire — minimum: `pathologyService.listCriticalUnacknowledged`, `prescriptionRepository.findByPatient`, `messageRepository.getInbox`/`listThreads`, `taskRepository.findMany`, FHIR Bundle responses (Condition/MedicationStatement/AllergyIntolerance/EpisodeOfCare/Practitioner). When `rows.length === <cap>` the response body MUST signal "this is bounded — there may be more"; without it consumers (clinician dashboard, AI agent, FHIR client) cannot distinguish "exactly N rows" from "≥ N truncated". Surfaced by BUG-437 L3+L4 review. Strong recommendation, non-blocking for BUG-437 but required before staging exit. Implementation: response wrapper `{ data, truncated: bool, displayedCount, message }`. |
| BUG-499 | S2 | FHIR `whereNull('deleted_at')` gap + non-deterministic ordering on `/Condition` (fhirRoutes.ts:100) and `/MedicationStatement` (fhirRoutes.ts:125). Tables `diagnoses` + `patient_medications` BOTH carry `deleted_at` per CLAUDE.md §1.4 — current FHIR routes return soft-deleted rows. Combined with the BUG-437 cap=500 (no `orderBy(...)`), the 500-row sample returned to FHIR clients is **non-deterministic across calls** when the underlying set exceeds 500. Fix shape: add `.whereNull('deleted_at')` to F1 + F2 to match F3/F4 + add `.orderBy('created_at', 'desc')` for stable iteration. Surfaced by BUG-437 L5 review. |
| BUG-500 | S3 | aiEnhancer.ts LLM-context section headers should signal cap-truncation. When `patient_medications:active` returns exactly 50 rows (BUG-437 A3 cap = 50) the `CURRENT MEDICATIONS (50)` header reads as "patient has exactly 50 meds" to the LLM. For polypharmacy patients with 51+ active meds the LLM-driven scribe reasons over a truncated set without knowing it. Fix shape: when `length === 50` render `CURRENT MEDICATIONS (50+ — truncated to most-recent 50 for LLM context budget)`. Same applies to A1 contacts, A2 episodes, A4 alerts, A5 legal_orders. Surfaced by BUG-437 L4 review (Rule 8 graceful-degradation lens). |
| BUG-501 | S3 | `taskRepository.findMany` ordering — currently `orderBy('t.due_date', 'asc').orderBy('t.created_at', 'desc')`. With the BUG-437 K1 cap = 500 an overdue HIGH-priority critical-followup task could theoretically be pushed past position 500 by 500 earlier-due LOW-priority tasks. Fix shape: `orderBy('t.priority', 'desc').orderBy('t.due_date', 'asc').orderBy('t.created_at', 'desc')` so HIGH-priority overdue surfaces first. Surfaced by BUG-437 L4 review (Rule 2). |
| BUG-502 | S3 | Single-run flake on `apps/api/tests/integration/limitCeilings.int.test.ts > F4 FHIR /Encounter cap=500` test. Across 5 consecutive `npm run test:integration` cycles run 2 returned 501 entries (cap not respected) while runs 1, 3, 4, 5 returned ≤ 500 GREEN. Hypothesis: vitest in-process module hot-reload artefact OR test-process state leak across the integration runner's per-file fork boundary. Other 7 cap=500 tests in the same file pass on every run, so the F4 transient does not invalidate the BUG-437 regression class — it surfaces only on local 5× rerun cycles, not single CI runs. Fix shape: investigate vitest module-isolation / consider explicit `vi.resetModules()` before each `it` block; confirm the integration runner's fresh-fork-per-file claim holds. Surfaced by BUG-437 §F flake-check + flagged by L3 absorb-1 reviewer as a follow-up. |
| ~~BUG-503~~ | **fixed** | ~~`discriminate()` in `apps/api/src/utils/authTokens.ts` does not enforce variant-internal invariants beyond distinguishing flags.~~ Closed 2026-05-24. `authTokens.discriminate()` now performs strict runtime claim validation and sanitised variant construction (patient-app requires `role='patient'`, rejects staff-only claims, rejects partial break-glass/impersonation claim sets). | BUG-504 | S3 | 5 redundant `req.user as { id: string; patientId?: string; clinicId?: string }` shape-narrow casts at `apps/api/src/features/patient-app/patientAppRoutes.ts:1000, 1059, 1092, 1127, 1208`. Now that BUG-463 lands the typed `AuthRequestUser` projection on `req.user` natively, these narrow casts are redundant. NOT in BUG-463's atomic scope (these are `as { ... }` not `as unknown as { ... }`), so the regression-trap regex doesn't fire. Fix shape: delete the 5 narrow casts; rely on the typed projection. | BUG-505 | S3 | Add static guard `scripts/guards/check-no-as-unknown-as-jwt-payload.ts` to extend coverage of the BUG-463 `as unknown as` JWT-payload regression-class to NEW files. Today the 3 `absent`-mode fix-registry rows cover only the 3 canonical middleware files (authMiddleware, breakGlassAuditMiddleware, adminImpersonationAuditMiddleware). A future engineer creating a new middleware that re-introduces the cast pattern would NOT be caught by the existing rows. Fix shape: a guard that scans `apps/api/src/{middleware,mcp,features}/**` for `(payload\|req\.user) as unknown as \{` patterns; allowlist the 2 ws-state-attachment casts in `scribeStreaming.ts:260,339` which are an unrelated WebSocket library convention. Surfaced by BUG-463 L5 review (soft follow-up #3) + matches CLAUDE.md §11 Layer-2-then-Layer-N strategy. |
| BUG-506 | S3 | CSP-report endpoint route-scoped body parser is INERT for Firefox `application/json` reports because the global `express.json({ limit: '2mb' })` at `apps/api/src/server.ts:351` consumes the body BEFORE `cspReportRoutes`'s 64KB-scoped parser fires. Effective limit is 2MB for Firefox, 64KB for Chrome's `application/csp-report` MIME. Not a security failure (2MB is still bounded; rate-limited; Zod-validated; legitimate reports < 2KB), but the route-author's intent of a stricter 64KB cap is unrealised on the Firefox path. Fix shape: mount `cspReportRoutes` BEFORE `app.use(express.json({ limit: '2mb' }))` so the route-scoped parser always wins for both MIMEs. Requires re-ordering the public-route-band mount in server.ts. Surfaced by BUG-468 L3 + L5 reviews. |

| BUG-626 | **fixed** | ~~(BUG-622 L4 cascade-discovery; surfaced 2026-04-29) DEFENCE-IN-DEPTH GAP — `medication_administrations.patient_medication_id` is currently nullable at the DB layer (verified live: column carries `Nullable: <empty>` indicating nullable). BUG-622 closes the field-name drift via Zod (Layer A) only — `MedicationAdministrationCreateSchema.patientMedicationId: z.string().uuid()` enforces non-null at the request boundary. But a future writer that bypasses Zod (admin tool, raw SQL, retrospective backfill, integration import, BUG-623 fix that doesn't go through Zod) could re-introduce NULL writes. The structural fix would be `ALTER COLUMN patient_medication_id SET NOT NULL` after backfilling any pre-existing NULL legacy rows (see BUG-629 for the data-quality audit). Caveat: the FK has `ON DELETE SET NULL` semantics — if the parent `patient_medications` row is deleted, the administration's `patient_medication_id` WOULD become NULL. Two options: (a) keep ON DELETE SET NULL + accept nullable column; (b) change to ON DELETE RESTRICT + enforce NOT NULL — more aggressive but consistent with append-only clinical record discipline (you can't delete a patient_medications row without first archiving its administrations). Decision deferred to design review. S2 because Layer A (Zod) is the contract and is enforced; Layer C (DB) is belt below the contract; Layer B (service) is implicit via Zod. Filed atomically with BUG-622 per `feedback_no_silent_out_of_scope.md`.~~ — Closed atomically: NEW migration `apps/api/migrations/20260430010000_bug_626_medication_administrations_patient_medication_id_not_null.ts` does TWO things: (1) ALTER COLUMN patient_medication_id SET NOT NULL on `medication_administrations`; (2) ALTER FK from ON DELETE SET NULL → ON DELETE RESTRICT, blocking deletion of a parent `patient_medications` row while administrations exist (CLAUDE.md §17 append-only clinical record discipline). Audit query (recorded in migration JSDoc): `SELECT COUNT(*) FILTER (WHERE patient_medication_id IS NULL) FROM medication_administrations` returned 0 — no backfill required, no operator decision needed (closes BUG-629 atomically). Migration applied as Batch 50; schema-snapshot regenerated. Zod Response schema updated: `patientMedicationId: z.string().uuid()` (no `.nullable()`). MedicationAdministrationRow interface updated: `patient_medication_id: string` (no `\| null`). | BUG-637-FOLLOWUP-MULTI-CONDITION | S2 | (BUG-637 cycle-2 self-cascade; surfaced 2026-04-29) The FK-aware-join guard's regex captures only 3-arg Knex joins (`.innerJoin('table', 'leftCol', 'rightCol')`). The L3 cycle-1 reviewer found 17+ such call sites. Cycle-2 absorb added a WARN counter so the unvalidated surface size is auditable (currently 11 sites scanned). | BUG-637-FOLLOWUP-RAW-SQL | S2 | (BUG-637 self-cascade; surfaced 2026-04-29) The BUG-637 FK-aware join lint guard covers Knex builder calls (`.innerJoin`/`.leftJoin`/`.rightJoin`/`.fullOuterJoin`) but NOT raw SQL `JOIN ... ON ... = ...` patterns inside `db.raw()` / `dbRead.raw()` / `.whereRaw()` strings. BUG-623 + BUG-632 pre-fix were both raw-SQL JOIN patterns — the guard would NOT have caught either pre-fix shape. Post-fix both use Knex builder so the guard catches future regressions. Fix shape: extend the guard to parse `JOIN <table>(?:\s+(?:as\s+)?<alias>)?\s+ON\s+<col1>\s*=\s*<col2>` patterns inside raw-SQL strings (after stripping `${...}` interpolations), resolve table aliases (more complex than Knex builder because raw-SQL aliases can chain via `FROM ... JOIN ... JOIN ...`), and validate FK compatibility same as the Knex path. Filed atomically with BUG-637 per `feedback_no_silent_out_of_scope.md` to close the structural-prevention gap. |

| BUG-633 | S1 (DEFERRED) | (BUG-632 L4 cascade-discovery FINDING-1; surfaced 2026-04-29; deferred 2026-04-30 to BUG-633-FOLLOWUP-EXTRACT-SUB-ROUTERS) `apps/api/src/features/roles/nurseFeatureRoutes.ts:217-262` GET `/medications/due-now` — `bed_movements` LEFT JOIN filters `bm.movement_type='admission'` only. Does NOT pick the LATEST admission and does NOT exclude patients with a subsequent `discharge` row. A patient admitted to bed A → discharged → re-admitted to bed B will appear TWICE in the result, each row showing a different ward/bed_label. Clinical consequence: nurse sees the same scheduled dose listed twice on the due-now panel, possibly with the OLD bed location → either confusion (administer twice?) or going to the wrong bed. The canonical pattern lives at `apps/api/src/features/beds/bedRoutes.ts:55-75` (DISTINCT ON (bed_id) + NOT EXISTS later discharge). Fix shape: replace the simple LEFT JOIN with a LATERAL sub-select applying that pattern (~10 LOC). **DEFERRED**: nurseFeatureRoutes.ts is at 771 LOC = ceiling 722 + 50 grace - 1; the LATERAL sub-select would exceed grace. Per BUG-528 ratchet (one-way drops only), the structural answer is to extract sub-routers (BUG-524-style: nurse-mar.ts + nurse-handover.ts + nurse-observations.ts). BUG-633 fix lands in the sub-router extraction cycle (BUG-633-FOLLOWUP-EXTRACT-SUB-ROUTERS). Filed atomically with BUG-632 per `feedback_no_silent_out_of_scope.md`. |

| BUG-553-FOLLOWUP-DSP-RECONCILE | S2 | (BUG-553 cycle-2 follow-up; surfaced via L4 CONCERN-1 2026-05-01) When `prescriptionService.cancel` succeeds locally but the DSP-side `escriptService.cancelToken` call fails (NPDS down, eRx REST 5xx, or NPDS not configured), the prescription row is `status='cancelled'` but the corresponding `erx_tokens` row remains `status='issued'` and the DSP still considers the token live — pharmacies may still dispense until reconciliation. The service emits a structured warn-log `kind: 'ERX_CANCEL_DSP_FAILED'` carrying `prescriptionId + tokenId + clinicId + error`. The UI surfaces this to the clinician via an alert telling them to contact the pharmacy directly. **Fix shape**: NEW reconciliation cron (sibling of existing schedulers in `apps/api/src/jobs/schedulers/`) that runs every ~15min, queries `prescriptions WHERE status='cancelled' AND is_electronic=true` JOINed against `erx_tokens WHERE status='issued'`, retries `escriptService.cancelToken` for each, and on success flips the token. On 5+ retry failures emit a SEV2 alert to oncall + clinician. Cron must be `dbAdmin` from inception per BUG-583 lesson. Belt-and-braces: existing dispensing-event webhook from NPDS continues to surface dispensed_at; reconciliation focuses on closing the active-token window. Filed atomically per `feedback_no_silent_out_of_scope.md`. |
| BUG-PR-R1-24-CASCADE-DRAIN-TIMER-TRY-CATCH | S2 | (PR-R1-24 implementation cascade; surfaced 2026-05-01; preventive — baseline is 0 violations) UMBRELLA CASCADE (currently EMPTY): both known async timer sites in `apps/api/src/` (`mcp/scribeStreaming.ts:273` cleanupInterval + `jobs/bootstrap.ts:183` healthCheckTimer) already wrap their callback body in try/catch per CLAUDE.md §3.2 (verified by initial scan). PR-R1-24 guard wires the discipline into CI so NEW async timer callbacks without try/catch are mechanically rejected. The umbrella row exists for symmetry and as the catalogue location should a future regression require an entry. Allowlist `scripts/guards/check-timer-try-catch.allowlist` is empty. | BUG-PR-R1-24-FOLLOWUP-FIRST-STATEMENT-TRY | S3 | (PR-R1-24 v1 lenience documented 2026-05-01) The PR-R1-24 guard accepts ANY `try {` block in the callback body, including nested ones inside an `if`/`else` branch. A timer that wraps only PART of its work (e.g., `if (cond) { try { await foo(); } catch {} } await bar();`) would currently PASS even though `await bar()` is outside the try and would crash the process on rejection. The 2 known sites both wrap their entire body so the lenience is currently inert. Future tighter check: require the body's FIRST non-comment statement to be `try {` (or document `// @timer-try-catch-partial: <reason>` for legitimate partial-wrapping). Estimated 4-6h to implement + add adversarial fixtures. Filed atomically per `feedback_no_silent_out_of_scope.md`. |

| BUG-447-FOLLOWUP-NOTECARD-KEYDOWN-BUBBLE | S3 | (BUG-447-clinical-notes-scribe L3+L4 retroactive-cycle-2 follow-up; surfaced by independent reviewers on a344b23) `apps/web/src/features/clinical-notes/components/NoteCard.tsx:90-95` inner amend `<IconButton>` carries `onClick={(e) => { e.stopPropagation(); onAmend(note); }}` to prevent click-bubble to the Card's onClick. Post-fix the Card now also has an `onKeyDown` handler (Shape B trio) that calls `select(note)`. When a keyboard-only clinician focuses the inner amend IconButton and presses Enter/Space: (1) IconButton's onClick fires (stopPropagation correctly prevents click-bubble); (2) keydown event STILL bubbles to Card's onKeyDown (React SyntheticEvent does NOT auto-stop on native-button keydown). Result: both `onAmend(note)` AND `select(note)` fire on a single Enter press. **Clinical consequence: NIL** — `select()` is read-only client state (note becomes selected in side panel; no DB write, no PHI movement); amend modal opens on top regardless. The commit message at a344b23 claimed React 18 doesn't bubble keydown which is technically incorrect; the latent double-fire has zero clinical-decision side-effect today because `handleSelectNote` is purely read-only. **Defence-in-depth fix (LEGACY prescription, superseded 2026-04-28)**: add `onKeyDown={(e) => { if (e.key === 'Enter' || e.key === ' ') e.stopPropagation(); }}` to the inner amend IconButton — OR — guard Card's onKeyDown with `if (e.target !== e.currentTarget) return;`. **GOLD-STANDARD fix (canonical 2026-04-28 onwards, per BUG-447-FOLLOWUP-SHAPE-B-PRIME-DOC L5 advisory)**: migrate NoteCard from Shape B trio (whole-Card-as-button) to Shape B′ (sub-region trigger + sibling actions). The amend IconButton becomes a sibling of an inner `<Box component="button" type="button">` trigger; the keydown-bubble class is eliminated structurally rather than defended-against. NoteCard is the ONLY legacy Shape-B-with-nested-IconButton site; the cascade-1e rule (BUG-447-CASCADE-1e, when it lands) will catch any future re-introduction. Filed atomically with retroactive verification of a344b23 per `feedback_no_silent_out_of_scope.md`; prescription updated 2026-04-28 to harvest the SSoT landed by SHAPE-B-PRIME-DOC. |

| BUG-447-FOLLOWUP-APPOINTMENTS-PARSEINT-RADIX | **fixed** | ~~(BUG-447-appointments L1 cascade-discovery follow-up; surfaced 2026-04-28 during full 28-guard L1 verification of child 8/15)~~ — `apps/web/src/features/patients/components/detail/tabs/AppointmentsTab.tsx:197+220` carried `parseInt(a.startTime)` without explicit radix in two slot-filter `.filter(a => parseInt(a.startTime) === hour)` lambdas (introduced 2026-03-28 in commit ^1432767). Both blocked the naming-conventions guard (Rule 4). The slot's `a.startTime` is always an `HH:MM` string (e.g. `"09:00"`); leading zeros on the hour part mean `parseInt('08', undefined)` interprets as octal in legacy engines (returns 0 for `"08"` and `"09"` historically). In modern V8 leading-zero is treated as decimal, but the lint guard fires regardless. Clinical consequence: in legacy octal-parse engines, the 08:00 + 09:00 hour rows would mis-bucket to the 0 hour and disappear from the day view — a real (rare today) appointment-display bug. Closed atomically as part of BUG-447-appointments because (a) the discovery happened during this cycle's L1 sweep, (b) per PART 3 cascade-discovery protocol the cascade folds into the cycle BEFORE the cycle's commit lands, (c) splitting into a separate cycle for two-character fixes would be process theatre. Fix: `parseInt(a.startTime)` → `parseInt(a.startTime, 10)` at both sites. |
| BUG-447-CASCADE-1e | S2 | (BUG-447-correspondence-letters L5 architecture-reviewer cascade follow-up; filed 2026-04-28) Extend `eslint-plugins/signacare-rules/rules/no-onclick-on-mui-container.js` to detect a NEW structural variant: a `<Box role="button" tabIndex={0} onKeyDown=...>` that ENCLOSES another keyboard-accessible primitive (`<IconButton>` / `<Button>` / `<MenuItem>` / `<Chip onClick>`). The current cascade-1 rule catches "MUI container with onClick that's not keyboard-accessible"; cascade-1e catches "MUI container that IS keyboard-accessible but contains another keyboard-accessible primitive (the ARIA nested-button anti-pattern)". Distinct rule, distinct class. Today's letter-card refactor (Shape B′) avoids this anti-pattern by making the trigger sibling-of-IconButton, but the static rule cannot today guarantee future Shape B′ implementations don't re-create the problem. The rule extension is the structural defence that pins Shape B′ correctness. **Acceptance**: rule fires on `<Box|Paper|Card|Typography role="button" tabIndex={0} onKeyDown=...>` whose subtree contains `<Button>` / `<IconButton>` / `<MenuItem>` / `<Chip onClick=>`. Allowlist of false-positives (e.g. submit-button-inside-form-disclosure-pattern) is the campaign discipline established in BUG-447-CASCADE-1. Filed atomically per `feedback_no_silent_out_of_scope.md`. |

---

## How to use this document

1. When planning the next commit, pick the highest-severity `state: open` item that is NOT `blocked_external` / `deferred`, unless an explicit gate is documented.
2. Every ship of a bug MUST: (a) move the row out of its section into "Shipped this session" AND update `docs/archive/audit-2026-04-19/bug-catalogue-v2.yaml` state in the same commit, OR (b) delete the "Shipped" entry and update the yaml — one of the two.
3. Catalogue drift is tracked as BUG-CATALOGUE-SYNC; any discovered drift moves the affected entry into the S2 section of this document until reconciled.
